	<h1 id="firstHeading" class="firstHeading" lang="en">KPMG</h1>
	
	<div id="bodyContent" class="mw-body-content">
		<div id="siteSub" class="noprint">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>

<p><b>KPMG International Cooperative</b> (or simply <b>KPMG</b>) is a <a href="/wiki/Professional_service" class="mw-redirect" title="Professional service">multinational professional services</a> network, and one of the <a href="/wiki/Big_Four_accounting_firms" title="Big Four accounting firms">Big Four</a> accounting organizations.  
</p><p>Seated in <a href="/wiki/Amstelveen" title="Amstelveen">Amstelveen</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Netherlands" title="Netherlands">Netherlands</a>, KPMG is a network of firms in 147 countries, with over 219,000 employees and has three lines of services: <a href="/wiki/Financial_audit" title="Financial audit">financial audit</a>, tax, and <a href="/wiki/Management_consulting" title="Management consulting">advisory</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-globalrevenuesfy19_4-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-globalrevenuesfy19-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup> Its tax and advisory services are further divided into various service groups.
</p><p>The name "KPMG" stands for "Klynveld Peat Marwick Goerdeler". It was chosen when KMG (Klynveld Main Goerdeler) merged with Peat Marwick in 1987.
</p>

<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:345_park1.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a9/345_park1.jpg/220px-345_park1.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="404" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a9/345_park1.jpg/330px-345_park1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/a/a9/345_park1.jpg 2x" data-file-width="371" data-file-height="681" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:345_park1.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Headquarters of KPMG LLP, the United States-based member firm of KPMG International, at 345 Park Avenue, New York City, USA</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Montreal_KPMG_Tower.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/de/Montreal_KPMG_Tower.jpg/220px-Montreal_KPMG_Tower.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="293" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/de/Montreal_KPMG_Tower.jpg/330px-Montreal_KPMG_Tower.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/de/Montreal_KPMG_Tower.jpg/440px-Montreal_KPMG_Tower.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2736" data-file-height="3648" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Montreal_KPMG_Tower.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The 34-story <a href="/wiki/KPMG_Tower" title="KPMG Tower">KPMG Tower</a> on De Maisonneuve Boulevard in Montreal, Quebec, Canada</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:KPMG_Tower.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/70/KPMG_Tower.jpg/220px-KPMG_Tower.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="282" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/70/KPMG_Tower.jpg/330px-KPMG_Tower.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/70/KPMG_Tower.jpg/440px-KPMG_Tower.jpg 2x" data-file-width="468" data-file-height="600" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:KPMG_Tower.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The KPMG Tower at 355 South Grand Avenue in <a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles" title="Los Angeles">Los Angeles</a>, <a href="/wiki/California" title="California">California</a>, USA</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:150wjeff.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/68/150wjeff.jpg/220px-150wjeff.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="294" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/68/150wjeff.jpg/330px-150wjeff.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/68/150wjeff.jpg/440px-150wjeff.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2132" data-file-height="2848" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:150wjeff.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>KPMG offices at 150 West Jefferson in Detroit, Michigan, USA</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:KPMGBayAdelaide.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/28/KPMGBayAdelaide.jpg/220px-KPMGBayAdelaide.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="330" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/28/KPMGBayAdelaide.jpg/330px-KPMGBayAdelaide.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/28/KPMGBayAdelaide.jpg/440px-KPMGBayAdelaide.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1627" data-file-height="2440" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:KPMGBayAdelaide.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>KPMG at the Bay Adelaide West tower in <a href="/wiki/Toronto" title="Toronto">Toronto</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ontario" title="Ontario">Ontario</a>, Canada</div></div></div>
<p>The organization's history has spanned three centuries. In 1818 John Moxham opened a company in <a href="/wiki/Bristol" title="Bristol">Bristol</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Chartered_Accountants_in_England_and_Wales:_A_Guide_to_Historical_Records_1-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Chartered_Accountants_in_England_and_Wales:_A_Guide_to_Historical_Records-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup> James Grace and James Grace Jr. bought John Moxham &amp; Co. and renamed it James Grace &amp; Son in 1857.<sup id="cite_ref-Chartered_Accountants_in_England_and_Wales:_A_Guide_to_Historical_Records_1-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Chartered_Accountants_in_England_and_Wales:_A_Guide_to_Historical_Records-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup> In 1861 Henry Grace joined James Jr. and the company was renamed James &amp; Henry Grace; the firm evolved to become Grace, Ryland &amp; Co.<sup id="cite_ref-Chartered_Accountants_in_England_and_Wales:_A_Guide_to_Historical_Records_1-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Chartered_Accountants_in_England_and_Wales:_A_Guide_to_Historical_Records-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/William_Barclay_Peat" title="William Barclay Peat">William Barclay Peat</a> joined Robert Fletcher &amp; Co. in London in 1870 at the age of 17 and became head of the firm in 1891, renamed William Barclay Peat &amp; Co. by then.<sup id="cite_ref-history_5-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-history-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> In 1877 Thomson McLintock founded Thomson McLintock &amp; Co in Glasgow.<sup id="cite_ref-history_5-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-history-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> In 1897 Marwick Mitchell &amp; Co. was founded by James Marwick and Roger Mitchell in New York City. In 1899 Ferdinand William LaFrentz founded the American Audit Co., in New York.<sup id="cite_ref-New_York_State_Society_of_Certified_Public_Accountants:_Foundation_of_a_Profession_6-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-New_York_State_Society_of_Certified_Public_Accountants:_Foundation_of_a_Profession-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> In 1923 The American Audit Company was renamed FW LaFrentz &amp; Co.<sup id="cite_ref-New_York_State_Society_of_Certified_Public_Accountants:_Foundation_of_a_Profession_6-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-New_York_State_Society_of_Certified_Public_Accountants:_Foundation_of_a_Profession-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In about 1913, Frank Wilber Main founded Main &amp; Co. in Pittsburgh.<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup> In March 1917 <a href="/wiki/Piet_Klijnveld" title="Piet Klijnveld">Piet Klijnveld</a> and Jaap Kraayenhof opened an accounting firm called <a href="/wiki/Klynveld_Kraayenhof_%26_Co." title="Klynveld Kraayenhof &amp; Co.">Klynveld Kraayenhof &amp; Co.</a> in Amsterdam.<sup id="cite_ref-history_5-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-history-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 1925 William Barclay Peat &amp; Co. and Marwick Mitchell &amp; Co., merged to form Peat Marwick Mitchell.<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 1963 Main LaFrentz &amp; Co was formed by the merger of Main &amp; Co and FW LaFrentz &amp; Co. In 1969 Thomson McLintock and Main LaFrentz merged forming McLintock Main LaFrentz International <sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> and McLintock Main LaFrentz International absorbed the general practice of Grace, Ryland &amp; Co.<sup id="cite_ref-Chartered_Accountants_in_England_and_Wales:_A_Guide_to_Historical_Records_1-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Chartered_Accountants_in_England_and_Wales:_A_Guide_to_Historical_Records-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 1979 <a href="/wiki/Klynveld_Kraayenhof_%26_Co." title="Klynveld Kraayenhof &amp; Co.">Klynveld Kraayenhof &amp; Co.</a> (Netherlands), McLintock Main LaFrentz (United Kingdom / United States) and Deutsche Treuhandgesellschaft (Germany) formed KMG (Klynveld Main Goerdeler) as a grouping of independent national practices to create a strong European-based international firm.<sup id="cite_ref-history_5-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-history-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> Deutsche Treuhandgesellschaft CEO <a href="/wiki/Reinhard_Goerdeler" title="Reinhard Goerdeler">Reinhard Goerdeler</a> (son of leading anti-Nazi activist <a href="/wiki/Carl_Friedrich_Goerdeler" title="Carl Friedrich Goerdeler">Carl Goerdeler</a>, who would have become Chancellor if <a href="/wiki/Operation_Valkyrie" title="Operation Valkyrie">Operation Valkyrie</a> had succeeded) became the first CEO of KMG.  In the United States, Main Lafrentz &amp; Co. merged with Hurdman and Cranstoun to form Main Hurdman &amp; Cranstoun.<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Then in 1987 KMG and Peat Marwick joined forces in the first mega-merger of large accounting firms and formed a firm called KPMG in the United States, and most of the rest of the world, and Peat Marwick McLintock in the United Kingdom.<sup id="cite_ref-history_5-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-history-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In the Netherlands, as a consequence of the merger between PMI and KMG in 1988, PMI tax advisors joined Meijburg &amp; Co. (The tax advisory agency Meijburg &amp; Co. was founded by Willem Meijburg, Inspector of National Taxes, in 1939). Today, the Netherlands is the only country with two members of KPMG International: KPMG Audit (accountants) and Meijburg &amp; Co (tax consultants).<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 1991 the firm was renamed KPMG Peat Marwick, and in 1999 the name was reduced again to KPMG.<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In October 1997, KPMG and <a href="/wiki/Ernst_%26_Young" title="Ernst &amp; Young">Ernst &amp; Young</a> announced that they were to merge.<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup> However, while the merger to form <a href="/wiki/PricewaterhouseCoopers" title="PricewaterhouseCoopers">PricewaterhouseCoopers</a> was granted regulatory approval, the KPMG/Ernst &amp; Young tie-up was later abandoned.<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Recent_history">Recent history</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=KPMG&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Recent history">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:KPMG_in_Kamloops,_Canada.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f9/KPMG_in_Kamloops%2C_Canada.jpg/220px-KPMG_in_Kamloops%2C_Canada.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f9/KPMG_in_Kamloops%2C_Canada.jpg/330px-KPMG_in_Kamloops%2C_Canada.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f9/KPMG_in_Kamloops%2C_Canada.jpg/440px-KPMG_in_Kamloops%2C_Canada.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2122" data-file-height="1414" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:KPMG_in_Kamloops,_Canada.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>KPMG building in <a href="/wiki/Kamloops" title="Kamloops">Kamloops</a>, <a href="/wiki/British_Columbia" title="British Columbia">British Columbia</a>, Canada</div></div></div>
<p>In 2001 KPMG divested its U.S. consulting firm through an <a href="/wiki/Initial_public_offering" title="Initial public offering">initial public offering</a> of <a href="/wiki/KPMG_Consulting_Inc" class="mw-redirect" title="KPMG Consulting Inc">KPMG Consulting Inc</a>, which is now called <a href="/wiki/BearingPoint" title="BearingPoint">BearingPoint, Inc.</a><sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> In early 2009, BearingPoint filed for Chapter 11 bankruptcy protection.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The UK and Dutch consulting arms were sold to <a href="/wiki/Atos_Origin" class="mw-redirect" title="Atos Origin">Atos Origin</a> in 2002.<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2003 KPMG divested itself of its legal arm, Klegal<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup> and KPMG LLP sold its Dispute Advisory Services to <a href="/wiki/FTI_Consulting" title="FTI Consulting">FTI Consulting</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>KPMG's member firms in the United Kingdom, Germany, Switzerland and Liechtenstein merged to form KPMG Europe LLP in October 2007. These member firms were followed by Spain, Belgium, the Netherlands, Luxembourg, <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_of_Independent_States" title="Commonwealth of Independent States">CIS</a> (Azerbaijan, Russia, Ukraine, Belarus, Kyrgyzstan, Kazakhstan, Armenia and Georgia), Turkey, Norway, and Saudi Arabia.<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup> They appointed joint Chairmen, John Griffith-Jones and Ralf Nonnenmacher.<sup id="cite_ref-history_5-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-history-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Global_structure">Global structure</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=KPMG&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Global structure">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Each national KPMG firm is an independent legal entity and is a member of KPMG International Cooperative, a Swiss entity registered in the Swiss <a href="/wiki/Canton_of_Zug" title="Canton of Zug">Canton of Zug</a>. KPMG International changed its legal structure from a <a href="/wiki/Swiss_Verein" class="mw-redirect" title="Swiss Verein">Swiss Verein</a> to a <a href="/wiki/Co-operative" class="mw-redirect" title="Co-operative">co-operative</a> under Swiss law in 2003.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>This structure in which the Cooperative provides support services only to the member firms is similar to other <a href="/wiki/Professional_services_networks" class="mw-redirect" title="Professional services networks">professional services networks</a>. The member firms provide the services to client. The purpose is to limit the liability of each independent member.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Bill Thomas is KPMG's Global Chairman.  He was formerly Senior Partner and CEO of KPMG LLP, the KPMG member firm in Canada.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Some KPMG member firms are registered as multidisciplinary entities which also provide legal services in certain jurisdictions.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In <a href="/wiki/India" title="India">India</a>, regulations do not permit foreign auditing firms to operate.<sup id="cite_ref-et_28-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-et-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup> Hence KPMG carries out audits in India under the name of BSR &amp; Co, an auditing firm that it bought. BSR &amp; Co was an auditing firm founded by B.S. Raut in Mumbai. In 1992, after India was forced to <a href="/wiki/Economic_liberalisation_in_India" title="Economic liberalisation in India">liberalise</a> as one of the conditions of the <a href="/wiki/World_Bank" title="World Bank">World Bank</a> and <a href="/wiki/IMF" class="mw-redirect" title="IMF">IMF</a> <a href="/wiki/Bail_out" class="mw-redirect" title="Bail out">bail out</a>, KPMG was granted a license to operate in India as an <a href="/wiki/Investment_bank" class="mw-redirect" title="Investment bank">investment bank</a>. It subsequently purchased BSR &amp; Co and conducts audits in India under the name of this firm.<sup id="cite_ref-ie29sep_29-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ie29sep-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Services">Services</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=KPMG&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Services">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>KPMG is organised into the following three service lines (the 2018 revenue shares are listed in parentheses):<sup id="cite_ref-globalrevenuesfy18_30-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-globalrevenuesfy18-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Audit" title="Audit">Audit</a> (39%)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Management_consulting" title="Management consulting">Advisory</a> (39%)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Tax_advisor" title="Tax advisor">Tax</a> (22%)</li></ul>
<p>Tax arrangements relating to <a href="/wiki/Tax_avoidance" title="Tax avoidance">tax avoidance</a> and multinational corporations and Luxembourg which were negotiated by KPMG became public in 2014 in the so-called <i><a href="/wiki/Luxembourg_Leaks" title="Luxembourg Leaks">Luxembourg Leaks</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Staff">Staff</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=KPMG&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Staff">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>KPMG was the preferred employer among the Big Four accounting firms according to CollegeGrad.com.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup> It was also ranked No. 4 on the list of "50 Best Places to Launch a Career" in 2009 according to <a href="/wiki/Bloomberg_Businessweek" title="Bloomberg Businessweek">Bloomberg Businessweek</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2009, in the United Kingdom, KPMG introduced a programme known as 'Flexible Futures'. This allowed staff to volunteer to give the firm the option to either send them on a <a href="/wiki/Sabbatical" title="Sabbatical">sabbatical</a> at 30% pay for up to 12 weeks, or to reduce their working hours to 4 days a week. The option remained open to the firm until October 2010. This facility has been invoked by the firm in some departments. KPMG publicised this as innovative and an alternative approach to redundancies.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>It was reported in early 2012 that KPMG has about 11,000 staff in the UK and 9,000 in mainland China and Hong Kong. KPMG's global deputy chairman predicted that headcount in China would overtake that of the UK by the end of 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>KPMG's Innovation Lab is based out of a <a href="/wiki/WeWork" title="WeWork">WeWork</a> in New York City.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Controversies">Controversies</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=KPMG&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Controversies">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tax_shelter_fraud">Tax shelter fraud</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=KPMG&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Tax shelter fraud">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/KPMG_tax_shelter_fraud" title="KPMG tax shelter fraud">KPMG tax shelter fraud</a></div>
<p>In 2003, the IRS issued summonses to KPMG for information about certain tax shelters and their investors.<sup id="cite_ref-NYT280805_37-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYT280805-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup> In February 2004, the US Justice Department commenced a criminal inquiry.<sup id="cite_ref-NYT280805_37-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYT280805-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup> The United States member firm, KPMG LLP, was accused by the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Department_of_Justice" title="United States Department of Justice">United States Department of Justice</a> of fraud in marketing abusive tax shelters. KPMG fired or forced the retirement of over a dozen who were involved.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup> KPMG LLP admitted criminal wrongdoing in creating fraudulent tax shelters to help wealthy clients avoid $2.5 billion in taxes between 1996 and 2002, and agreed to pay $456 million in penalties to avoid indictment. Under the <a href="/wiki/Deferred_prosecution_agreement" class="mw-redirect" title="Deferred prosecution agreement">deferred prosecution agreement</a>, KPMG LLP would not face criminal prosecution if it complied with the terms of its agreement with the government. On 3 January 2007, the criminal conspiracy charges against KPMG were dropped.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Various">Various</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=KPMG&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Various">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In 2003, KPMG agreed to pay $125 million and $75 million to settle lawsuits stemming from the firm's audits of <a href="/wiki/Rite_Aid" title="Rite Aid">Rite Aid</a> and Oxford Health Plans Inc., respectively.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2004, KPMG agreed to pay $115 million to settle lawsuits stemming from the collapse of software company <a href="/wiki/Lernout_%26_Hauspie" title="Lernout &amp; Hauspie">Lernout &amp; Hauspie</a> Speech Products NV.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2006, <a href="/wiki/Fannie_Mae" title="Fannie Mae">Fannie Mae</a> sued KPMG for malpractice for approving years of erroneous <a href="/wiki/Financial_statement" title="Financial statement">financial statements</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In February 2007, KPMG Germany was investigated for ignoring questionable payments in the <a href="/wiki/Siemens" title="Siemens">Siemens</a> bribery case.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup> In November 2008, the Siemens Supervisory Board recommended changing auditors from KPMG to Ernst &amp; Young.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In March 2008, KPMG was accused of enabling "improper and imprudent practices" at <a href="/wiki/New_Century_Financial" class="mw-redirect" title="New Century Financial">New Century Financial</a>, a failed mortgage company,<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup> and KPMG agreed to pay $80 million to settle suits from <a href="/wiki/Xerox" title="Xerox">Xerox</a> shareholders over manipulated earnings reports.<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>It was announced in December 2008 that two of <a href="/wiki/Tremont_Group" title="Tremont Group">Tremont Group</a>'s Rye Select funds, audited by KPMG, had $2.37 billion invested with the <a href="/wiki/Bernard_Madoff" class="mw-redirect" title="Bernard Madoff">Madoff</a> "<a href="/wiki/Ponzi_scheme" title="Ponzi scheme">Ponzi scheme</a>."<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup> Class action suits were filed.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In August 2010, it was reported by the Swedish Financial Supervisory Authority to the Swedish accountancy regulator after HQ Bank was forced into involuntary liquidation after the Financial Supervisory Authority revoked all its licences for breach of banking regulations.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In August 2011, KPMG conducted due diligence work on <a href="/wiki/Hewlett_Packard" class="mw-redirect" title="Hewlett Packard">Hewlett Packard</a>'s $11.1 billion acquisition of the British software company <a href="/wiki/Autonomy_Corporation" class="mw-redirect" title="Autonomy Corporation">Autonomy</a>. In November 2012 HP announced an $8.8 billion write off due to "serious accounting improprieties" committed by Autonomy management prior to the acquisition.<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>According to an independent panel formed to investigate irregular payments made by <a href="/wiki/Olympus_Corporation" title="Olympus Corporation">Olympus</a> which reported in December 2011, KPMG's affiliate in Japan did not identify fraud at the company.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In April 2013, Scott London, a former KPMG LLP partner in charge of KPMG's US Los Angeles-based Pacific Southwest audit practice, admitted passing on stock tips about clients, including <a href="/wiki/Herbalife" class="mw-redirect" title="Herbalife">Herbalife</a>, <a href="/wiki/Skechers" title="Skechers">Skechers</a>, and other companies, to his friend Bryan Shaw, a California jewelry-store owner.<sup id="cite_ref-gpkpmg_54-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gpkpmg-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup> In return Shaw gave London $70,000 as well as gifts that included a $12,000 Rolex watch and concert tickets.<sup id="cite_ref-wsj9_55-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wsj9-55">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-gpkpmg_54-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gpkpmg-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup> On May 6, Shaw agreed to plead guilty to one count of conspiracy to commit <a href="/wiki/Securities_fraud" title="Securities fraud">securities fraud</a>. He also agreed to pay around $1.3 million in restitution, and to cooperate with the government as part of a plea deal with federal prosecutors.<sup id="cite_ref-R9_56-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-R9-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup> This scandal led KPMG to resign as auditor for Herbalife and Sketchers.<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2015, KPMG was accused by the <a href="/wiki/Canada_Revenue_Agency" title="Canada Revenue Agency">Canada Revenue Agency</a> of tax evasion schemes: "The CRA alleges that the KPMG tax structure was in reality a 'sham' that intended to deceive the taxman."<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2016, the Canada Revenue Agency was found to have offered an amnesty to KPMG clients caught using an offshore tax-avoidance scheme on the <a href="/wiki/Isle_of_Man" title="Isle of Man">Isle of Man</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2017, KPMG terminated five partners in its audit practice, including the head of its audit practice in the US, after an investigation of advanced confidential knowledge of planned audit inspections by its <a href="/wiki/Public_Company_Accounting_Oversight_Board" title="Public Company Accounting Oversight Board">Public Company Accounting Oversight Board</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Dealbook_KPMG_fires_6_61-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Dealbook_KPMG_fires_6-61">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup> This followed criticism about KPMG's failure to uncover illegal sales practices at <a href="/wiki/Wells_Fargo" title="Wells Fargo">Wells Fargo</a> or potential corruption at <a href="/wiki/FIFA" title="FIFA">FIFA</a>, the governing international body of football.<sup id="cite_ref-Dealbook_KPMG_fires_6_61-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Dealbook_KPMG_fires_6-61">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup> It was reported in 2017 that KPMG had the highest number of deficiencies, among the <a href="/wiki/Big_Four_accounting_firms" title="Big Four accounting firms">Big Four</a>, cited by its regulator in the previous two years.<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup> This includes two annual inspections that were compromised as a result of advanced access to inspection information. In March 2019, David Middendorf and Jeffrey Wada, co-defendants in the scandal, were convicted.<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2017, KPMG paid a $6.2 million fine to the <a href="/wiki/US_Securities_and_Exchange_Commission" class="mw-redirect" title="US Securities and Exchange Commission">US Securities and Exchange Commission</a> for inadequacies in its audit of the financial statements of oil and gas company, Miller Energy Resources.<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In November 2017, 91 partners of KPMG faced contempt proceedings in <a href="/wiki/Hong_Kong_High_Court" class="mw-redirect" title="Hong Kong High Court">Hong Kong High Court</a>, as <a href="/wiki/China_Medical_Technologies" title="China Medical Technologies">China Medical Technologies</a> (CMED) liquidators investigating a $400 million fraud took action against KPMG with regard to its refusal honor a February 2016 court order to produce Chinese working papers, correspondence, and records to the liquidators.<sup id="cite_ref-II_65-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-II-65">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated6_66-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated6-66">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup> The liquidators are asking that 91 defendants be held in <a href="/wiki/Contempt_of_court" title="Contempt of court">contempt of court</a>, which could result in criminal penalties, or weekly fines.<sup id="cite_ref-II_65-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-II-65">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup>  KPMG had issued written audit reports for CMED from 2003 to 2008, and was replaced by <a href="/wiki/PwC" class="mw-redirect" title="PwC">PwC</a> Zhong Tian in August 2009.<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated6_66-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated6-66">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup> "Perhaps locking up 91 KPMG partners over Christmas may spur the firms to find a solution to this problem", said Professor Paul Gillis of <a href="/wiki/Peking_University" title="Peking University">Peking University</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Guanghua_School_of_Management" title="Guanghua School of Management">Guanghua School of Management</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-II_65-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-II-65">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In November 2018, the <a href="/wiki/Sultanate_of_Oman" class="mw-redirect" title="Sultanate of Oman">Sultanate of Oman</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Muscat_Securities_Market" title="Muscat Securities Market">Capital Market Authority (CMA)</a> suspended KPMG from auditing entities regulated by the CMA for a period of one year after discovering major financial and accounting irregularities in the entities' records.<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-McCance-15Nov2018_72-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-McCance-15Nov2018-72">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2019 KPMG were fined Â£5 million by the <a href="/wiki/Financial_Reporting_Council" title="Financial Reporting Council">Financial Reporting Council</a> for misconduct shortly after the takeover of the <a href="/wiki/Britannia_Building_Society" title="Britannia Building Society">Britannia Building Society</a> by <a href="/wiki/The_Co-operative_Bank" title="The Co-operative Bank">The Co-operative Bank</a>, particularly relating to the valuation of Britannia's commercial loans and other liabilities. The takeover led to the near collapse of The Co-operative Bank.<sup id="cite_ref-guardian-20190508_73-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-guardian-20190508-73">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Carillion_audit_role">Carillion audit role</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=KPMG&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Carillion audit role">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In January 2018, it was announced that KPMG, auditor of collapsed UK construction firm <a href="/wiki/Carillion" title="Carillion">Carillion</a>, would have its role examined by the <a href="/wiki/Financial_Reporting_Council" title="Financial Reporting Council">Financial Reporting Council</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup> (FRC) and it was summoned to give evidence before two House of Commons select committees on 22 February 2018.<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 13 February 2018, the 'Big 4' accountancy firms, including KPMG, were described by MP <a href="/wiki/Frank_Field_(British_politician)" title="Frank Field (British politician)">Frank Field</a> as "feasting on what was soon to become a carcass" after collecting fees of Â£72m for Carillion work during the years leading up to its collapse.<sup id="cite_ref-Davies-13Feb2018_76-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Davies-13Feb2018-76">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup> KPMG was singled out for particular criticism for signing off Carillion's last accounts before a profit warning in July 2017: "Either KPMG failed to spot the warning signs, or its judgement was clouded by its cosy relationship with the company and the multimillion-pound fees it received," said MP <a href="/wiki/Rachel_Reeves" title="Rachel Reeves">Rachel Reeves</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Davies-13Feb2018_76-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Davies-13Feb2018-76">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup> Two out of three former Carillion finance directors had also worked for KPMG.<sup id="cite_ref-Davies-13Feb2018_76-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Davies-13Feb2018-76">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>KPMG defended itself, saying that in the construction industry "an accumulation of adverse events [...] can quite quickly cause a precipitous decline." KPMG chairman and senior partner Bill Michael said: "It does not follow automatically from a company collapse either that the opinion of management was wrong, or that the auditor did a bad job."<sup id="cite_ref-Davies-13Feb2018_76-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Davies-13Feb2018-76">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 22 February 2018, MPs contested evidence from KPMG (in one exchange MP <a href="/wiki/Peter_Kyle_(politician)" class="mw-redirect" title="Peter Kyle (politician)">Peter Kyle</a> told KPMG partner Peter Meehan: "I would not hire you to do an audit of the contents of my fridge").<sup id="cite_ref-Marriage-22Feb2018_77-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Marriage-22Feb2018-77">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup> Rachel Reeves, chair of the business select committee, said:
</p>
<blockquote><p>Auditing is a multi-million-pound business for the Big Four. On this morning's evidence from KPMG and Deloitte, these audits appear to be a colossal waste of time and money, fit only to provide false assurance to investors, workers and the public. [...] Carillion staff and investors could see the problems at the company but those responsible - auditors, regulators, and, ultimately, the directors â€“ did nothing to stop Carillion being driven off a cliff.<sup id="cite_ref-ParlUK-22Feb2018_78-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ParlUK-22Feb2018-78">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup></p></blockquote>
<p>The final report of the Parliamentary inquiry into Carillion's collapse, published on 16 May 2018,<sup id="cite_ref-Davies-16May2018_79-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Davies-16May2018-79">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup> criticised KPMG for its "complicity" in the company's financial reporting practices:
</p>
<blockquote><p>KPMG audited Carillion for 19 years, pocketing Â£29 million in the process. Not once during that time did they qualify their audit opinion on the financial statements, instead signing off the figures put in front of them by the company's directors. Yet, had KPMG been prepared to challenge management, the warning signs were there in highly questionable assumptions about construction contract revenue and the intangible asset of goodwill accumulated in historic acquisitions. These assumptions were fundamental to the picture of corporate health presented in audited annual accounts. In failing to exerciseâ€”and voiceâ€”professional scepticism towards Carillion's aggressive accounting judgements, KPMG was complicit in them. It should take its own share of responsibility for the consequences.<sup id="cite_ref-Carillion_report_conclusion_80-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Carillion_report_conclusion-80">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup></p></blockquote>
<p>The select committee chairs (Frank Field and Rachel Reeves) called for a complete overhaul of Britain's corporate governance regime, saying the government had "lacked the decisiveness or bravery" to do so, accused the big four accounting firms of operating as a "cosy club", with KPMG singled out for its "complicity" in signing off Carillion's "increasingly fantastical figures".<sup id="cite_ref-Davies-16May2018_79-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Davies-16May2018-79">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>KPMG said:
</p>
<blockquote><p>We believe we conducted our audit appropriately. However, it's only right that following a corporate collapse of such size and significance, the necessary investigations are performed. Auditing large and complex businesses involves many judgments and we will continue to cooperate with the FRC's ongoing investigation. ... We welcome any future review of our profession. If we consider how the profession has changed in the last decade [â€¦] it is clear there is a need for us to look closely at our business models.<sup id="cite_ref-Davies-16May2018_79-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Davies-16May2018-79">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup></p></blockquote>
<p>In a June 2018 report on audit standards across eight accounting firms, the FRC identified "failure to challenge management and show appropriate scepticism across their audits." It highlighted a decline in the quality of work undertaken by the Big Four, with KPMG performing the worst. There had, the FRC said, been an "unacceptable deterioration" in the quality of KPMG's work, and the FRC would scrutinise KPMG more closely as a result.<sup id="cite_ref-Davies-18Jun2018_81-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Davies-18Jun2018-81">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup> In October 2018, the FRC proposed reforms to tackle the "underlying falling trust in business and the effectiveness of audit," and severely rebuked KPMG.<sup id="cite_ref-Collinson-8Oct2018_82-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Collinson-8Oct2018-82">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In November 2018, KPMG said it would no longer undertake consultancy work for <a href="/wiki/FTSE_350_Index" title="FTSE 350 Index">FTSE 350 Index</a>-listed companies if it was also auditing them, in an effort to "remove even the perception of a possible conflict" of interest.<sup id="cite_ref-BBC-09Nov2018_83-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBC-09Nov2018-83">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The Carillion investigation followed FRC investigations into KPMG's role at <a href="/wiki/HBOS" title="HBOS">HBOS</a>, Quindell and <a href="/wiki/The_Co-operative_Bank" title="The Co-operative Bank">The Co-operative Bank</a>. In July 2018, the FRC started an investigation into KPMG's audit role at collapsed drinks merchant <a href="/wiki/Bargain_Booze" title="Bargain Booze">Conviviality</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Vincent-3Jul2018_84-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Vincent-3Jul2018-84">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In January 2019, KPMG announced it had suspended the partner that led Carillion's audit and three members of his team,<sup id="cite_ref-Morby-21Jan2019_85-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Morby-21Jan2019-85">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup> and the FRC opened a second investigation into how KPMG audited Carillion's accounts.<sup id="cite_ref-Jones-22Jan2019_86-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Jones-22Jan2019-86">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Alterations_to_past_audit_work">Alterations to past audit work</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=KPMG&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Alterations to past audit work">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In June 2019, KPMG was fined $50 million for altering its past audit work after receiving stolen data from accounting industry watch dog Public Company Accounting Oversight Board (PCAOB). KPMG admitted to its mistakes and as a part of its settlement, it also agreed to hire an independent consultant to review its internal controls.<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2017_South_African_corruption_scandal">2017 South African corruption scandal</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=KPMG&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: 2017 South African corruption scandal">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Gupta_family#Uranium_interests,_Nhlanhla_Nene,_Pravin_Gordhan_and_KPMG" title="Gupta family">Gupta family Â§&#160;Uranium interests, Nhlanhla Nene, Pravin Gordhan and KPMG</a></div>
<p>In 2017, KPMG was embroiled in related scandals involving the <a href="/wiki/Gupta_family" title="Gupta family">Gupta family</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup> KPMG, whose history in South Africa dated back to 1895, and which had been part of the international organization since its founding in 1979,<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup> faced calls for closure, and an uncertain future, as a consequence of the damage done to the South African economy as a result of its activities.<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>KPMG had been working with a Gupta family company in the mining sector, Oakbay Resources and Energy, for 15 years prior to the revelations of corruption and collusion in 2016, at which point KPMG resigned. The full impact and financial profit that KPMG received is yet to be determined;<sup id="cite_ref-timesKPMG_92-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-timesKPMG-92">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup> however, at least one large company has terminated its services with KPMG due to its relationship with Oakbay.<sup id="cite_ref-mgKPMG1_93-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mgKPMG1-93">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In July 2017, after controversial documents were leaked by the amaBhungane Centre for Investigative Journalism, former chief executive of KPMG South Africa and the former partner that was responsible for audits related to the Gupta family, Moses Kgosana, withdrew from becoming the chairman of <a href="/wiki/Alexander_Forbes_Group_Holdings" title="Alexander Forbes Group Holdings">Alexander Forbes</a>, a financial services firm.<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">&#91;95&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2015, KPMG issued a controversial report that implicated former Finance Minister <a href="/wiki/Pravin_Gordhan" title="Pravin Gordhan">Pravin Gordhan</a> in the creation of an illegal intelligence gathering unit of the <a href="/wiki/South_African_Revenue_Service" title="South African Revenue Service">South African Revenue Service</a> (SARS). This report was seen by elements of the media to be part of a wider Gupta-linked <a href="/wiki/State_capture" title="State capture">state capture</a> conspiracy, with the aim of forcing Gordhan out of his post.<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup> The report was withdrawn by KPMG in September 2017,<sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">&#91;97&#93;</a></sup> earning the ire of the Commissioner of SARS, Tom Moyane.<sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>After an internal investigation that found work done for the Gupta family fell "considerably short" of the firm's standards and amid rising political and public backlash, KPMG's senior leadership in South Africa, including its chairman Ahmed Jaffer, CEO Trevor Hoole, COO Steven Louw, and five partners, resigned in September 2017.<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">&#91;99&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">&#91;100&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Save South Africa, a civil-society group, accused KPMG and UK PR firm <a href="/wiki/Bell_Pottinger" title="Bell Pottinger">Bell Pottinger</a> of playing a "central role in facilitating state capture."<sup id="cite_ref-Cotterill-15Sep2017_101-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cotterill-15Sep2017-101">&#91;101&#93;</a></sup> Numerous South African companies either fired KPMG in the immediate aftermath of the scandal, or were reconsidering their relationships with the firm <sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">&#91;102&#93;</a></sup> with the international chairman of KPMG, John Veihmeyer, apologising for the conduct of the South African arm<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">&#91;103&#93;</a></sup> and the firm pledged to donate fees earned from Gupta businesses, as well as the withdrawn SARS report to anti-corruption activities.<sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">&#91;104&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Sponsorship">Sponsorship</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=KPMG&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Sponsorship">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:The_Squaire,_Frankfurt_am_Main-1060.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f9/The_Squaire%2C_Frankfurt_am_Main-1060.jpg/220px-The_Squaire%2C_Frankfurt_am_Main-1060.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="124" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f9/The_Squaire%2C_Frankfurt_am_Main-1060.jpg/330px-The_Squaire%2C_Frankfurt_am_Main-1060.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f9/The_Squaire%2C_Frankfurt_am_Main-1060.jpg/440px-The_Squaire%2C_Frankfurt_am_Main-1060.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4849" data-file-height="2728" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:The_Squaire,_Frankfurt_am_Main-1060.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>KPMG Europe headquarters in <a href="/wiki/The_Squaire" title="The Squaire">the Squaire</a> building at <a href="/wiki/Frankfurt_Airport" title="Frankfurt Airport">Frankfurt Airport</a></div></div></div>
<p>The Swedish member firm was main sponsor for Swedish <a href="/wiki/Biathlon" title="Biathlon">biathlete</a> <a href="/wiki/Magdalena_Forsberg" title="Magdalena Forsberg">Magdalena Forsberg</a>, six-time world champion and two-time Olympic medalist. Forsberg was working as a tax consultant at the KPMG <a href="/wiki/Sundsvall" title="Sundsvall">Sundsvall</a> office parallel to her athletic career.<sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105">&#91;105&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In February 2008, <a href="/wiki/Phil_Mickelson" title="Phil Mickelson">Phil Mickelson</a>, ranked one of the best golfers in the world, signed a three-year global sponsorship deal with KPMG. As part of the agreement, Mickelson was to wear the KPMG logo on his headwear during all golf related appearances.<sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">&#91;106&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The Canadian member firm sponsored skier <a href="/wiki/Alexandre_Bilodeau" title="Alexandre Bilodeau">Alexandre Bilodeau</a>, who won the first gold medal for Canada on home soil in the <a href="/wiki/2010_Vancouver_Olympics" class="mw-redirect" title="2010 Vancouver Olympics">2010 Vancouver Olympics</a>. Alexandre's father is a tax partner in the Montreal office.<sup id="cite_ref-Bilodeau_107-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bilodeau-107">&#91;107&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-GoingConcern_108-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GoingConcern-108">&#91;108&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>KPMG and <a href="/wiki/McLaren_Technology_Group" class="mw-redirect" title="McLaren Technology Group">McLaren Technology Group</a> have formed a strategic alliance to apply <a href="/wiki/McLaren_Applied_Technologies" title="McLaren Applied Technologies">McLaren Applied Technologies</a>' (MAT) <a href="/wiki/Predictive_analytics" title="Predictive analytics">predictive analytics</a> and technology to KPMG's audit and advisory services. McLaren 2015 Formula 1 car has the KPMG logo engraved above the pilot seat.<sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">&#91;109&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Since 2016, KPMG has been strategic sponsor of <a href="/wiki/Brain_Bar" title="Brain Bar">Brain Bar</a>, a Budapest-based, annually held festival on the future.<sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">&#91;110&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Awards">Awards</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=KPMG&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Awards">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>KPMG ranked in the top two overall in Consultancy Rankings 2009 by OpRisk &amp; Compliance â€“ in recognition of KPMG's experience in risk management.<sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111">&#91;111&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2011, the company was ranked second on the World's Best Outsourcing Advisors â€“ in recognition of the firm's depth of experience, global reach and holistic approach.<sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">&#91;112&#93;</a></sup> That same year, the company was inducted into Working Mother Hall of Fame after being honored for 15 years as one of Working Mother magazine's 100 Best Companies for Working Mothers.<sup id="cite_ref-workingmother_113-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-workingmother-113">&#91;113&#93;</a></sup> KPMG was ranked number 13 in <i>Consulting Magazine'</i>s Best Firms to Work for in 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114">&#91;114&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2017, KPMG was ranked 29th on <i>Fortune</i> list of 100 best companies to work for.<sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115">&#91;115&#93;</a></sup> That same year, KPMG, along with <a href="/wiki/PricewaterhouseCoopers" title="PricewaterhouseCoopers">PwC</a>, <a href="/wiki/Deloitte" title="Deloitte">Deloitte</a>, and <a href="/wiki/PA_Consulting_Group" title="PA Consulting Group">PA Consulting Group</a>, were among the UK's 25 top companies to work for.<sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116">&#91;116&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
